"""
SOC RT Ticket Auto-Close Script (CLI Only)
-----------------------------------------
Automatically checks open RT tickets in the SOC Alerts queue
and closes them if the related alert has been cleared.

🛠️ Features:
- Fetches all open RT tickets.
- Checks the latest comment for "clear" keywords.
- If cleared, resolves & closes the ticket automatically.
- Logs all actions in Logs/SOC_RTs_Log.txt.
✅ Fully automated with error handling. Designed for CLI operation.
"""

import logging
import os
import sys

# Debugging message to confirm script execution
print("DEBUG: close_cleared_rts.py started...")

# Ensure Utils is accessible for rt_api.py
BASE_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))  # Get script directory
UTILS_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Utils")  # Locate Utils folder
sys.path.append(UTILS_DIR)  # Add to system path

import rt_api  # RT API wrapper

# ✅ Setup Logging in Logs Directory
LOG_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Logs")
os.makedirs(LOG_DIR, exist_ok=True)  # Create Logs directory if missing
LOG_FILE = os.path.join(LOG_DIR, "SOC_RTs_Log.txt")

logging.basicConfig(filename=LOG_FILE, format='%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s', level=logging.INFO)

print("DEBUG: Logging initialized...")  # Debugging output


# 🔧 RT API Configuration
RT_QUEUE = "SOC Alerts"  # Adjust if necessary

# ✅ Keywords used to identify a cleared alert
CLEAR_KEYWORDS = ["cleared", "alert cleared", "resolved", "no further action needed"]


def get_open_tickets():
    """Fetches open alert tickets from RT."""
    logging.info("🔍 Fetching open alert tickets from RT...")

    try:
        tickets = rt_api.get_open_tickets(RT_QUEUE)
        logging.info(f"✅ Found {len(tickets)} open alert tickets.")
        return tickets
    except Exception as e:
        logging.error(f"❌ Error retrieving RT tickets: {e}")
        return []


def is_alert_cleared(ticket_id):
    """Checks if the latest comment on an RT ticket indicates the alert is cleared."""
    logging.info(f"🔎 Checking RT ticket #{ticket_id} for cleared alert status...")

    try:
        latest_comment = rt_api.get_latest_ticket_comment(ticket_id)

        if not latest_comment:
            logging.info(f"⚠️ No recent comments found for RT ticket #{ticket_id}. Assuming NOT cleared.")
            return False

        latest_comment = latest_comment.strip().lower()

        if any(keyword in latest_comment for keyword in CLEAR_KEYWORDS):
            logging.info(f"✅ Alert in RT ticket #{ticket_id} is cleared.")
            return True
        else:
            logging.info(f"❌ Alert in RT ticket #{ticket_id} is NOT cleared.")
            return False

    except Exception as e:
        logging.error(f"❌ Error checking alert status for RT ticket #{ticket_id}: {e}")
        return False


def close_ticket(ticket_id):
    """Resolves and closes an RT ticket if the alert is cleared."""
    logging.info(f"🔒 Resolving RT ticket #{ticket_id}...")

    try:
        rt_api.resolve_ticket(ticket_id)
        rt_api.add_comment_to_ticket(ticket_id, "✅ Alert has been cleared. Auto-closing ticket.")
        logging.info(f"✅ RT ticket #{ticket_id} has been successfully closed.")
    except Exception as e:
        logging.error(f"❌ Error closing RT ticket #{ticket_id}: {e}")


def process_tickets():
    """Processes all open RT tickets and closes those with cleared alerts."""
    tickets = get_open_tickets()

    if not tickets:
        logging.info("✅ No open RT tickets found. Exiting...")
        return

    for ticket_id in tickets:
        if is_alert_cleared(ticket_id):
            close_ticket(ticket_id)

    logging.info("✅ All cleared RT tickets processed successfully!")


if __name__ == "__main__":
    process_tickets()




"""
RT API Helper Module (CLI-Only)
-----------------------------------------
Provides helper functions to interact with the RT (Request Tracker) API.

🛠️ Features:
- Adds comments to RT tickets.
- Fetches ticket details.
- Retrieves open SOC tickets.
- Checks latest ticket comments.
- Resolves tickets.
- Logs all interactions in Logs/SOC_RT_API_Log.txt.

✅ Designed for easy integration with SOC scripts.
✅ Ensures error handling and logging.
"""

import requests
import logging
import os

# ✅ Setup Logging in Logs Directory
BASE_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))  # Get script directory
LOG_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "..", "Logs")  # Store logs in central location
os.makedirs(LOG_DIR, exist_ok=True)  # Create Logs directory if missing
LOG_FILE = os.path.join(LOG_DIR, "SOC_RT_API_Log.txt")

logging.basicConfig(filename=LOG_FILE, format='%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s', level=logging.INFO)

# 🔧 RT API Configuration
RT_URL = "https://rt.marchex.com/REST/1.0"
RT_USER = "socbot"
RT_PASS = "securepass"
RT_QUEUE = "SOC Alerts"  # Default queue

def _send_request(method, endpoint, data=None):
    """
    Sends an authenticated request to the RT API.

    Args:
        method (str): "GET" or "POST".
        endpoint (str): The RT API endpoint (e.g., "/ticket/1234/show").
        data (dict, optional): Data to send with the request.

    Returns:
        dict: Response data if successful, None otherwise.
    """

    url = f"{RT_URL}{endpoint}"
    try:
        if method == "GET":
            response = requests.get(url, auth=(RT_USER, RT_PASS), timeout=10)
        elif method == "POST":
            response = requests.post(url, auth=(RT_USER, RT_PASS), data=data, timeout=10)
        else:
            logging.error(f"❌ Invalid HTTP method: {method}")
            return None

        if response.status_code == 200:
            return response.text
        else:
            logging.error(f"❌ RT API request failed: {response.text}")
            return None

    except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
        logging.error(f"❌ Request error: {e}")
        return None


def add_comment(ticket_number, comment):
    """
    Adds a comment to an RT ticket.

    Args:
        ticket_number (str): The RT ticket number.
        comment (str): The comment content to be added.

    Returns:
        bool: True if successful, False otherwise.
    """

    if not ticket_number:
        logging.warning("⚠️ No RT ticket number provided. Skipping comment.")
        return False

    if not comment.strip():
        logging.warning(f"⚠️ Empty comment for RT Ticket #{ticket_number}. Skipping.")
        return False

    logging.info(f"📝 Attempting to comment on RT Ticket #{ticket_number}...")

    response = _send_request("POST", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/comment", {"content": comment})

    if response:
        logging.info(f"✅ Successfully commented on RT Ticket #{ticket_number}")
        return True
    else:
        logging.error(f"❌ Failed to comment on RT Ticket #{ticket_number}.")
        return False


def get_ticket_details(ticket_number):
    """
    Retrieves details of an RT ticket.

    Args:
        ticket_number (str): The RT ticket number.

    Returns:
        str: Ticket details if successful, None otherwise.
    """

    if not ticket_number:
        logging.warning("⚠️ No RT ticket number provided. Skipping request.")
        return None

    logging.info(f"📋 Fetching details for RT Ticket #{ticket_number}...")

    return _send_request("GET", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/show")


def get_open_tickets(queue_name=RT_QUEUE):
    """
    Fetches all open tickets in a given RT queue.

    Args:
        queue_name (str, optional): The RT queue name (default: "SOC Alerts").

    Returns:
        list: List of open ticket IDs, or an empty list if none found.
    """

    logging.info(f"🔍 Fetching open tickets in RT queue '{queue_name}'...")

    response = _send_request("GET", f"/search/ticket?query=Queue='{queue_name}' AND Status='open'")

    if response:
        tickets = [line.split(":")[0] for line in response.split("\n") if line.strip()]
        logging.info(f"✅ Found {len(tickets)} open tickets in queue '{queue_name}'.")
        return tickets
    else:
        logging.error(f"❌ Failed to fetch open tickets from queue '{queue_name}'.")
        return []


def get_latest_ticket_comment(ticket_number):
    """
    Retrieves the latest comment from an RT ticket.

    Args:
        ticket_number (str): The RT ticket number.

    Returns:
        str: Latest comment content if available, otherwise None.
    """

    logging.info(f"🔎 Retrieving latest comment for RT Ticket #{ticket_number}...")

    response = _send_request("GET", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/history?format=l")

    if response:
        comments = response.split("\n")
        latest_comment = comments[-1] if comments else ""
        logging.info(f"✅ Latest comment retrieved for RT Ticket #{ticket_number}.")
        return latest_comment.strip()
    else:
        logging.error(f"❌ Failed to retrieve comments for RT Ticket #{ticket_number}.")
        return None


def resolve_ticket(ticket_number):
    """
    Resolves an RT ticket by setting its status to 'resolved'.

    Args:
        ticket_number (str): The RT ticket number.

    Returns:
        bool: True if successful, False otherwise.
    """

    if not ticket_number:
        logging.warning("⚠️ No RT ticket number provided. Skipping resolution.")
        return False

    logging.info(f"🔒 Attempting to resolve RT Ticket #{ticket_number}...")

    response = _send_request("POST", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/edit", {"Status": "resolved"})

    if response:
        logging.info(f"✅ Successfully resolved RT Ticket #{ticket_number}.")
        return True
    else:
        logging.error(f"❌ Failed to resolve RT Ticket #{ticket_number}.")
        return False


if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Example Usage (For Testing Purposes)
    print("Fetching open tickets...")
    open_tickets = get_open_tickets()
    print(f"Open Tickets: {open_tickets}")

    if open_tickets:
        first_ticket = open_tickets[0]
        print(f"Fetching details for ticket {first_ticket}...")
        print(get_ticket_details(first_ticket))

        print(f"Fetching latest comment for ticket {first_ticket}...")
        print(get_latest_ticket_comment(first_ticket))

        print(f"Resolving ticket {first_ticket}...")
        resolve_ticket(first_ticket)

"""
SOC RT Ticket Auto-Close Script (CLI Only)
-----------------------------------------
Automatically checks open RT tickets in the SOC Alerts queue
and closes them if the related alert has been cleared.

🛠️ Features:
- Fetches all open RT tickets.
- Checks the latest comment for "clear" keywords.
- If cleared, resolves & closes the ticket automatically.
- Logs all actions in Logs/SOC_RTs_Log.txt.
✅ Fully automated with error handling. Designed for CLI operation.
"""

import logging
import os
import sys

# ✅ Ensure input/output uses UTF-8 (prevents UnicodeEncodeError & DecodeError)
sys.stdout.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")
sys.stderr.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")
sys.stdin.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")

# Ensure Utils is accessible for rt_api.py
BASE_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))  # Get script directory
UTILS_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Utils")  # Locate Utils folder
sys.path.append(UTILS_DIR)  # Add to system path

import rt_api  # RT API wrapper

# ✅ Setup Logging in Logs Directory
LOG_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Logs")
os.makedirs(LOG_DIR, exist_ok=True)  # Create Logs directory if missing
LOG_FILE = os.path.join(LOG_DIR, "SOC_RTs_Log.txt")

logging.basicConfig(filename=LOG_FILE, format='%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s', level=logging.INFO)

# ✅ Keywords used to identify a cleared alert
CLEAR_KEYWORDS = ["cleared", "alert cleared", "resolved", "no further action needed"]

def get_open_tickets():
    """Fetches open alert tickets from RT."""
    print("🔍 Fetching open RT tickets...")
    tickets = rt_api.get_open_tickets()

    if tickets:
        print(f"✅ Found {len(tickets)} open RT tickets.")
    else:
        print("✅ No open RT tickets found.")

    return tickets

def is_alert_cleared(ticket_id):
    """Checks if the latest comment on an RT ticket indicates the alert is cleared."""
    logging.info(f"🔎 Checking RT ticket #{ticket_id} for cleared alert status...")

    try:
        latest_comment = rt_api.get_latest_ticket_comment(ticket_id)

        if not latest_comment:
            logging.info(f"⚠️ No recent comments found for RT ticket #{ticket_id}. Assuming NOT cleared.")
            return False

        latest_comment = latest_comment.strip().lower()

        # ✅ Check for both clear phrases
        if "the following has cleared:" in latest_comment or "severity: clear" in latest_comment:
            logging.info(f"✅ Alert in RT ticket #{ticket_id} is cleared.")
            return True
        else:
            logging.info(f"❌ Alert in RT ticket #{ticket_id} is NOT cleared.")
            return False

    except Exception as e:
        logging.error(f"❌ Error checking alert status for RT ticket #{ticket_id}: {e}")
        return False

def close_ticket(ticket_id):
    """Resolves and closes an RT ticket if the alert is cleared."""
    print(f"🔒 Closing RT ticket #{ticket_id}...")

    if rt_api.resolve_ticket(ticket_id):
        rt_api.add_comment(ticket_id, "✅ Alert has been cleared. Auto-closing ticket.")
        print(f"✅ RT ticket #{ticket_id} successfully closed.")
    else:
        print(f"❌ Failed to close RT ticket #{ticket_id}.")

def process_tickets():
    """Processes all open RT tickets and closes those with cleared alerts."""
    logging.info("🚀 Starting RT ticket processing...")
    
    # ✅ Fetch open tickets from the correct queue
    tickets = get_open_tickets()

    if not tickets:
        logging.info("✅ No open RT tickets found. Exiting...")
        print("✅ No open RT tickets found.")
        return

    # ✅ Debugging: Show all open ticket IDs being checked
    print(f"🔍 Checking {len(tickets)} open RT tickets...")
    logging.info(f"🔍 Checking {len(tickets)} open RT tickets...")

    for ticket_id in tickets:
        print(f"🔎 Checking RT Ticket #{ticket_id}...")
        
        if is_alert_cleared(ticket_id):
            print(f"✅ Closing RT Ticket #{ticket_id} (Alert Cleared)...")
            close_ticket(ticket_id)

    logging.info("✅ All cleared RT tickets processed successfully!")
    print("✔ RT Queue Processing Complete!")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    process_tickets()




"""
RT API Helper Module (CLI-Only)
-----------------------------------------
Provides helper functions to interact with the RT (Request Tracker) API.

🛠️ Features:
- Adds comments to RT tickets.
- Fetches ticket details.
- Retrieves open SOC tickets.
- Checks latest ticket comments.
- Resolves tickets.
- Logs all interactions in Logs/SOC_RT_API_Log.txt.

✅ Designed for CLI operation with SOC scripts.
"""

import requests
import logging
import os

# ✅ Setup Logging in Logs Directory
BASE_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))  # Get script directory
LOG_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "..", "Logs")  # Store logs in central location
os.makedirs(LOG_DIR, exist_ok=True)  # Create Logs directory if missing
LOG_FILE = os.path.join(LOG_DIR, "SOC_RT_API_Log.txt")

logging.basicConfig(filename=LOG_FILE, format='%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s', level=logging.INFO)

# 🔧 RT API Configuration
RT_URL = "https://rt.marchex.com/REST/1.0"
RT_USER = "socbot"
RT_PASS = "securepass"

def _send_request(method, endpoint, data=None):
    """
    Sends an authenticated request to the RT API.

    Args:
        method (str): "GET" or "POST".
        endpoint (str): The RT API endpoint.
        data (dict, optional): Request payload.

    Returns:
        str: Response text if successful, None otherwise.
    """
    url = f"{RT_URL}{endpoint}"

    try:
        response = requests.request(method, url, auth=(RT_USER, RT_PASS), data=data, timeout=10)

        if response.status_code == 200:
            return response.text
        else:
            logging.error(f"❌ RT API request failed: {response.text}")
            return None

    except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
        logging.error(f"❌ Request error: {e}")
        return None

def add_comment(ticket_number, comment):
    """Adds a comment to an RT ticket."""
    if not ticket_number or not comment.strip():
        logging.warning(f"⚠️ Missing ticket number or empty comment for RT Ticket #{ticket_number}.")
        return False

    response = _send_request("POST", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/comment", {"content": comment})
    return bool(response)

def get_ticket_details(ticket_number):
    """Retrieves details of an RT ticket."""
    return _send_request("GET", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/show")

def get_open_tickets(queue_name="Production"):
    """
    Fetches all open tickets in a given RT queue.

    Args:
        queue_name (str, optional): The RT queue name (default: "Production").

    Returns:
        list: List of open ticket IDs, or an empty list if none found.
    """

    logging.info(f"🔍 Fetching open tickets in RT queue '{queue_name}'...")

    # ✅ Ensure we fetch tickets that are 'open', 'new', or 'stalled'
    query = f"Queue='{queue_name}' AND (Status='open' OR Status='new' OR Status='stalled')"
    
    response = _send_request("GET", f"/search/ticket?query={query}")

    if response:
        # ✅ Extract ticket IDs from the RT response
        tickets = [line.split(":")[0].strip() for line in response.split("\n") if line.strip()]
        logging.info(f"✅ Found {len(tickets)} open tickets in queue '{queue_name}'.")
        return tickets
    else:
        logging.error(f"❌ Failed to fetch open tickets from queue '{queue_name}'.")
        return []

def get_latest_ticket_comment(ticket_number):
    """Retrieves the latest comment from an RT ticket."""
    response = _send_request("GET", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/history?format=l")
    return response.split("\n")[-1].strip() if response else None

def resolve_ticket(ticket_number):
    """Resolves an RT ticket by setting its status to 'resolved'."""
    return bool(_send_request("POST", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/edit", {"Status": "resolved"}))

if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Example test: fetch open tickets
    print("Fetching open tickets...")
    open_tickets = get_open_tickets()
    print(f"Open Tickets: {open_tickets}")

"""
SOC RT Ticket Auto-Close Script (CLI Only)
-----------------------------------------
Automatically checks open RT tickets in the SOC Alerts queue
and closes them if the related alert has been cleared.

🛠️ Features:
- Fetches all open RT tickets.
- Checks the latest comment for "clear" keywords.
- If cleared, resolves & closes the ticket automatically.
- Logs all actions in Logs/SOC_RTs_Log.txt.
✅ Fully automated with error handling. Designed for CLI operation.
"""

import logging
import os
import sys

# ✅ Ensure input/output uses UTF-8 (prevents UnicodeEncodeError & DecodeError)
sys.stdout.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")
sys.stderr.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")
sys.stdin.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")

# Ensure Utils is accessible for rt_api.py
BASE_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))  # Get script directory
UTILS_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Utils")  # Locate Utils folder
sys.path.append(UTILS_DIR)  # Add to system path

import rt_api  # RT API wrapper

# ✅ Setup Logging in Logs Directory
LOG_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Logs")
os.makedirs(LOG_DIR, exist_ok=True)  # Create Logs directory if missing
LOG_FILE = os.path.join(LOG_DIR, "SOC_RTs_Log.txt")

logging.basicConfig(filename=LOG_FILE, format='%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s', level=logging.INFO)

# ✅ Keywords used to identify a cleared alert
CLEAR_KEYWORDS = ["cleared", "alert cleared", "resolved", "no further action needed"]

def get_open_tickets():
    """Fetches open alert tickets from RT."""
    print("🔍 Fetching open RT tickets...")
    tickets = rt_api.get_open_tickets()

    if tickets:
        print(f"✅ Found {len(tickets)} open RT tickets.")
    else:
        print("✅ No open RT tickets found.")

    return tickets

def is_alert_cleared(ticket_id):
    """Checks if the latest comment on an RT ticket indicates the alert is cleared."""
    logging.info(f"🔎 Checking RT ticket #{ticket_id} for cleared alert status...")

    try:
        latest_comment = rt_api.get_latest_ticket_comment(ticket_id)

        if not latest_comment:
            logging.info(f"⚠️ No recent comments found for RT ticket #{ticket_id}. Assuming NOT cleared.")
            return False

        latest_comment = latest_comment.strip().lower()

        # ✅ Check for both clear phrases
        if "the following has cleared:" in latest_comment or "severity: clear" in latest_comment:
            logging.info(f"✅ Alert in RT ticket #{ticket_id} is cleared.")
            return True
        else:
            logging.info(f"❌ Alert in RT ticket #{ticket_id} is NOT cleared.")
            return False

    except Exception as e:
        logging.error(f"❌ Error checking alert status for RT ticket #{ticket_id}: {e}")
        return False

def close_ticket(ticket_id):
    """Resolves and closes an RT ticket if the alert is cleared."""
    print(f"🔒 Closing RT ticket #{ticket_id}...")

    if rt_api.resolve_ticket(ticket_id):
        rt_api.add_comment(ticket_id, "✅ Alert has been cleared. Auto-closing ticket.")
        print(f"✅ RT ticket #{ticket_id} successfully closed.")
    else:
        print(f"❌ Failed to close RT ticket #{ticket_id}.")

def process_tickets():
    """Processes all open RT tickets and closes those with cleared alerts."""
    logging.info("🚀 Starting RT ticket processing...")
    
    # ✅ Fetch open tickets from the correct queue
    tickets = get_open_tickets()

    if not tickets:
        logging.info("✅ No open RT tickets found. Exiting...")
        print("✅ No open RT tickets found.")
        return

    # ✅ Debugging: Show all open ticket IDs being checked
    print(f"🔍 Checking {len(tickets)} open RT tickets...")
    logging.info(f"🔍 Checking {len(tickets)} open RT tickets...")

    for ticket_id in tickets:
        print(f"🔎 Checking RT Ticket #{ticket_id}...")
        
        if is_alert_cleared(ticket_id):
            print(f"✅ Closing RT Ticket #{ticket_id} (Alert Cleared)...")
            close_ticket(ticket_id)

    logging.info("✅ All cleared RT tickets processed successfully!")
    print("✔ RT Queue Processing Complete!")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    process_tickets()




"""
RT API Helper Module (CLI-Only)
-----------------------------------------
Provides helper functions to interact with the RT (Request Tracker) API.

🛠️ Features:
- Adds comments to RT tickets.
- Fetches ticket details.
- Retrieves open SOC tickets.
- Checks latest ticket comments.
- Resolves tickets.
- Logs all interactions in Logs/SOC_RT_API_Log.txt.

✅ Designed for CLI operation with SOC scripts.
"""

import requests
import logging
import os

# ✅ Setup Logging in Logs Directory
BASE_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))  # Get script directory
LOG_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "..", "Logs")  # Store logs in central location
os.makedirs(LOG_DIR, exist_ok=True)  # Create Logs directory if missing
LOG_FILE = os.path.join(LOG_DIR, "SOC_RT_API_Log.txt")

logging.basicConfig(filename=LOG_FILE, format='%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s', level=logging.INFO)

# 🔧 RT API Configuration
RT_URL = "https://rt.marchex.com/REST/1.0"
RT_USER = "socbot"
RT_PASS = "securepass"

def _send_request(method, endpoint, data=None):
    """
    Sends an authenticated request to the RT API.

    Args:
        method (str): "GET" or "POST".
        endpoint (str): The RT API endpoint.
        data (dict, optional): Request payload.

    Returns:
        str: Response text if successful, None otherwise.
    """
    url = f"{RT_URL}{endpoint}"

    try:
        response = requests.request(method, url, auth=(RT_USER, RT_PASS), data=data, timeout=10)

        if response.status_code == 200:
            return response.text
        else:
            logging.error(f"❌ RT API request failed: {response.text}")
            return None

    except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
        logging.error(f"❌ Request error: {e}")
        return None

def add_comment(ticket_number, comment):
    """Adds a comment to an RT ticket."""
    if not ticket_number or not comment.strip():
        logging.warning(f"⚠️ Missing ticket number or empty comment for RT Ticket #{ticket_number}.")
        return False

    response = _send_request("POST", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/comment", {"content": comment})
    return bool(response)

def get_ticket_details(ticket_number):
    """Retrieves details of an RT ticket."""
    return _send_request("GET", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/show")

def get_open_tickets(queue_name="Production"):
    """
    Fetches all open tickets in a given RT queue.

    Args:
        queue_name (str, optional): The RT queue name (default: "Production").

    Returns:
        list: List of open ticket IDs, or an empty list if none found.
    """

    logging.info(f"🔍 Fetching open tickets in RT queue '{queue_name}'...")

    # ✅ Debug: Print the exact query being used
    query = f"Queue='{queue_name}' AND (Status='open' OR Status='new' OR Status='stalled')"
    print(f"📡 RT API Query: {query}")  # Debugging output

    response = _send_request("GET", f"/search/ticket?query={query}")

    if response:
        print(f"🔍 Raw API Response:\n{response}")  # ✅ Debugging: Print the full API response

        # ✅ Extract ticket IDs from the RT response
        tickets = [line.split(":")[0].strip() for line in response.split("\n") if line.strip()]
        logging.info(f"✅ Found {len(tickets)} open tickets in queue '{queue_name}'.")
        return tickets
    else:
        logging.error(f"❌ Failed to fetch open tickets from queue '{queue_name}'.")
        return []

def get_latest_ticket_comment(ticket_number):
    """Retrieves the latest comment from an RT ticket."""
    response = _send_request("GET", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/history?format=l")

    if response:
        comments = response.split("\n")
        latest_comment = comments[-1].strip() if comments else ""
        print(f"📝 Latest Comment for Ticket {ticket_number}: {latest_comment}")  # ✅ Debugging output
        return latest_comment
    else:
        logging.error(f"❌ Failed to retrieve comments for RT Ticket #{ticket_number}.")
        return None

def resolve_ticket(ticket_number):
    """Resolves an RT ticket by setting its status to 'resolved'."""
    return bool(_send_request("POST", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/edit", {"Status": "resolved"}))

if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Example test: fetch open tickets
    print("Fetching open tickets...")
    open_tickets = get_open_tickets()
    print(f"Open Tickets: {open_tickets}")

        comments = response.split("\n")
        latest_comment = comments[-1].strip() if comments else ""
        print(f"📝 Latest Comment for Ticket {ticket_number}: {latest_comment}")  # ✅ Debugging output
        return latest_comment
    else:
        logging.error(f"❌ Failed to retrieve comments for RT Ticket #{ticket_number}.")
        return None

def resolve_ticket(ticket_number):
    """Resolves an RT ticket by setting its status to 'resolved'."""
    return bool(_send_request("POST", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/edit", {"Status": "resolved"}))

if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Example test: fetch open tickets
    print("Fetching open tickets...")
    open_tickets = get_open_tickets()
    print(f"Open Tickets: {open_tickets}")

"""
SOC RT Ticket Auto-Close Script (CLI Only)
-----------------------------------------
Automatically checks open RT tickets in the SOC Alerts queue
and closes them if the related alert has been cleared.

🛠️ Features:
- Fetches all open RT tickets.
- Checks the latest comment for "clear" keywords.
- If cleared, resolves & closes the ticket automatically.
- Logs all actions in Logs/SOC_RTs_Log.txt.
✅ Fully automated with error handling. Designed for CLI operation.
"""

import logging
import os
import sys

# ✅ Ensure input/output uses UTF-8 (prevents UnicodeEncodeError & DecodeError)
sys.stdout.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")
sys.stderr.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")
sys.stdin.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")

# Ensure Utils is accessible for rt_api.py
BASE_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))  # Get script directory
UTILS_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Utils")  # Locate Utils folder
sys.path.append(UTILS_DIR)  # Add to system path

import rt_api  # RT API wrapper

# ✅ Setup Logging in Logs Directory
LOG_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Logs")
os.makedirs(LOG_DIR, exist_ok=True)  # Create Logs directory if missing
LOG_FILE = os.path.join(LOG_DIR, "SOC_RTs_Log.txt")

logging.basicConfig(filename=LOG_FILE, format='%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s', level=logging.INFO)

# ✅ Keywords used to identify a cleared alert
CLEAR_KEYWORDS = ["cleared", "alert cleared", "resolved", "no further action needed"]

def get_open_tickets():
    """Fetches open alert tickets from RT."""
    print("🔍 Fetching open RT tickets...")
    tickets = rt_api.get_open_tickets()

    if tickets:
        print(f"✅ Found {len(tickets)} open RT tickets.")
    else:
        print("✅ No open RT tickets found.")

    return tickets

def is_alert_cleared(ticket_id):
    """Checks if the latest comment on an RT ticket indicates the alert is cleared."""
    logging.info(f"🔎 Checking RT ticket #{ticket_id} for cleared alert status...")

    try:
        latest_comment = rt_api.get_latest_ticket_comment(ticket_id)

        if not latest_comment:
            logging.info(f"⚠️ No recent comments found for RT ticket #{ticket_id}. Assuming NOT cleared.")
            return False

        latest_comment = latest_comment.strip().lower()

        # ✅ Check for both clear phrases
        if "the following has cleared:" in latest_comment or "severity: clear" in latest_comment:
            logging.info(f"✅ Alert in RT ticket #{ticket_id} is cleared.")
            return True
        else:
            logging.info(f"❌ Alert in RT ticket #{ticket_id} is NOT cleared.")
            return False

    except Exception as e:
        logging.error(f"❌ Error checking alert status for RT ticket #{ticket_id}: {e}")
        return False

def close_ticket(ticket_id):
    """Resolves and closes an RT ticket if the alert is cleared."""
    print(f"🔒 Closing RT ticket #{ticket_id}...")

    if rt_api.resolve_ticket(ticket_id):
        rt_api.add_comment(ticket_id, "✅ Alert has been cleared. Auto-closing ticket.")
        print(f"✅ RT ticket #{ticket_id} successfully closed.")
    else:
        print(f"❌ Failed to close RT ticket #{ticket_id}.")

def process_tickets():
    """Processes all open RT tickets and closes those with cleared alerts."""
    logging.info("🚀 Starting RT ticket processing...")
    
    # ✅ Fetch open tickets from the correct queue
    tickets = rt_api.get_open_tickets(queue_name="SOC Alerts")

    if not tickets:
        logging.info("✅ No open RT tickets found. Exiting...")
        print("✅ No open RT tickets found.")
        return

    # ✅ Debugging: Show all open ticket IDs being checked
    print(f"🔍 Checking {len(tickets)} open RT tickets...")
    logging.info(f"🔍 Checking {len(tickets)} open RT tickets...")

    for ticket_id in tickets:
        print(f"🔎 Checking RT Ticket #{ticket_id}...")
        
        if is_alert_cleared(ticket_id):
            print(f"✅ Closing RT Ticket #{ticket_id} (Alert Cleared)...")
            close_ticket(ticket_id)

    logging.info("✅ All cleared RT tickets processed successfully!")
    print("✔ RT Queue Processing Complete!")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    process_tickets()




"""
RT API Helper Module (CLI-Only)
-----------------------------------------
Provides helper functions to interact with the RT (Request Tracker) API.

🛠️ Features:
- Adds comments to RT tickets.
- Fetches ticket details.
- Retrieves open SOC tickets.
- Checks latest ticket comments.
- Resolves tickets.
- Logs all interactions in Logs/SOC_RT_API_Log.txt.

✅ Designed for CLI operation with SOC scripts.
"""

import requests
import logging
import os

# ✅ Setup Logging in Logs Directory
BASE_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))  # Get script directory
LOG_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "..", "Logs")  # Store logs in central location
os.makedirs(LOG_DIR, exist_ok=True)  # Create Logs directory if missing
LOG_FILE = os.path.join(LOG_DIR, "SOC_RT_API_Log.txt")

logging.basicConfig(filename=LOG_FILE, format='%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s', level=logging.INFO)

# 🔧 RT API Configuration
RT_URL = "https://rt.marchex.com/REST/1.0"
RT_USER = "socbot"
RT_PASS = "securepass"

def _send_request(method, endpoint, data=None):
    """
    Sends an authenticated request to the RT API.

    Args:
        method (str): "GET" or "POST".
        endpoint (str): The RT API endpoint.
        data (dict, optional): Request payload.

    Returns:
        str: Response text if successful, None otherwise.
    """
    url = f"{RT_URL}{endpoint}"

    try:
        response = requests.request(method, url, auth=(RT_USER, RT_PASS), data=data, timeout=10)

        if response.status_code == 200:
            return response.text
        else:
            logging.error(f"❌ RT API request failed: {response.text}")
            return None

    except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
        logging.error(f"❌ Request error: {e}")
        return None

def add_comment(ticket_number, comment):
    """Adds a comment to an RT ticket."""
    if not ticket_number or not comment.strip():
        logging.warning(f"⚠️ Missing ticket number or empty comment for RT Ticket #{ticket_number}.")
        return False

    response = _send_request("POST", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/comment", {"content": comment})
    return bool(response)

def get_ticket_details(ticket_number):
    """Retrieves details of an RT ticket."""
    return _send_request("GET", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/show")

def get_open_tickets(queue_name="SOC Alerts"):
    """
    Fetches all open tickets in a given RT queue.

    Args:
        queue_name (str, optional): The RT queue name (default: "Soc Alerts").

    Returns:
        list: List of open ticket IDs, or an empty list if none found.
    """

    logging.info(f"🔍 Fetching open tickets in RT queue '{queue_name}'...")

    # ✅ Debug: Print the exact query being used
    query = f"Queue='{queue_name}' AND (Status='open' OR Status='new' OR Status='stalled')"
    print(f"📡 RT API Query: {query}")  # Debugging output

    response = _send_request("GET", f"/search/ticket?query={query}")


    if response:
        print(f"🔍 Raw API Response:\n{response}")  # ✅ Debugging: Print the full API response

        # ✅ Extract ticket IDs from the RT response
        tickets = [line.split(":")[0].strip() for line in response.split("\n") if line.strip()]
        logging.info(f"✅ Found {len(tickets)} open tickets in queue '{queue_name}'.")
        return tickets
    else:
        logging.error(f"❌ Failed to fetch open tickets from queue '{queue_name}'.")
        return []

def get_latest_ticket_comment(ticket_number):
    """Retrieves the latest comment from an RT ticket."""
    response = _send_request("GET", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/history?format=l")

    if response:
        comments = response.split("\n")
        latest_comment = comments[-1].strip() if comments else ""
        print(f"📝 Latest Comment for Ticket {ticket_number}: {latest_comment}")  # ✅ Debugging output
        return latest_comment
    else:
        logging.error(f"❌ Failed to retrieve comments for RT Ticket #{ticket_number}.")
        return None

def resolve_ticket(ticket_number):
    """Resolves an RT ticket by setting its status to 'resolved'."""
    return bool(_send_request("POST", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/edit", {"Status": "resolved"}))

if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Example test: fetch open tickets
    print("Fetching open tickets...")
    open_tickets = get_open_tickets()
    print(f"Open Tickets: {open_tickets}")

import logging
import os

RT_URL = "https://rt.marchex.com/REST/1.0"
RT_USER = "socbot"
RT_PASS = "securepass"

import requests
import ssl
import urllib3

# ✅ Disable SSL verification warnings
urllib3.disable_warnings(urllib3.exceptions.InsecureRequestWarning)

# ✅ Override SSL settings globally (allows weaker DH keys)
try:
    ssl_context = ssl.create_default_context()
    ssl_context.set_ciphers("DEFAULT:@SECLEVEL=1")  # Allow weak keys
    requests.packages.urllib3.util.ssl_.DEFAULT_CIPHERS = "DEFAULT:@SECLEVEL=1"
except Exception as e:
    print(f"⚠️ Failed to override SSL settings: {e}")
    
# ✅ Custom SSL context to allow weak DH keys
custom_ssl_context = ssl.create_default_context()
custom_ssl_context.set_ciphers("DEFAULT:@SECLEVEL=1")  # Allow weaker SSL keys

def _send_request(method, endpoint, data=None):
    """
    Sends an authenticated request to the RT API.

    Args:
        method (str): "GET" or "POST".
        endpoint (str): The RT API endpoint.
        data (dict, optional): Request payload.

    Returns:
        str: Response text if successful, None otherwise.
    """
    url = f"{RT_URL}{endpoint}"
    print(f"📡 Sending {method} request to: {url}")  # Debugging output

    try:
        response = requests.request(
            method,
            url,
            auth=(RT_USER, RT_PASS),
            data=data,
            timeout=10,
            verify=False  # ✅ Ignore SSL verification
        )

        # ✅ Debugging: Print the full HTTP response
        print(f"🔍 Response Status Code: {response.status_code}")
        print(f"🔍 Response Text:\n{response.text}")

        if response.status_code == 200:
            return response.text
        else:
            logging.error(f"❌ RT API request failed: {response.text}")
            return None

    except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
        logging.error(f"❌ Request error: {e}")
        print(f"❌ Request error: {e}")  # Debugging output
        return None

def add_comment(ticket_number, comment):
    """Adds a comment to an RT ticket."""
    if not ticket_number or not comment.strip():
        logging.warning(f"⚠️ Missing ticket number or empty comment for RT Ticket #{ticket_number}.")
        return False

    response = _send_request("POST", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/comment", {"content": comment})
    return bool(response)

"""
SOC RT Ticket Auto-Close Script (CLI Only)
-----------------------------------------
Automatically checks open RT tickets in the SOC Alerts queue
and closes them if the related alert has been cleared.

🛠️ Features:
- Fetches all open RT tickets.
- Checks the latest comment for "clear" keywords.
- If cleared, resolves & closes the ticket automatically.
- Logs all actions in Logs/SOC_RTs_Log.txt.
✅ Fully automated with error handling. Designed for CLI operation.
"""

import logging
import os
import sys

# ✅ Ensure input/output uses UTF-8 (prevents UnicodeEncodeError & DecodeError)
sys.stdout.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")
sys.stderr.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")
sys.stdin.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")

# Ensure Utils is accessible for rt_api.py
BASE_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))  # Get script directory
UTILS_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Utils")  # Locate Utils folder
sys.path.append(UTILS_DIR)  # Add to system path

import rt_api  # RT API wrapper

# ✅ Setup Logging in Logs Directory
LOG_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Logs")
os.makedirs(LOG_DIR, exist_ok=True)  # Create Logs directory if missing
LOG_FILE = os.path.join(LOG_DIR, "SOC_RTs_Log.txt")

logging.basicConfig(filename=LOG_FILE, format='%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s', level=logging.INFO)

# ✅ Keywords used to identify a cleared alert
CLEAR_KEYWORDS = ["cleared", "alert cleared", "resolved", "no further action needed"]

def get_open_tickets():
    """Fetches open alert tickets from RT."""
    print("🔍 Fetching open RT tickets...")
    tickets = rt_api.get_open_tickets()

    if tickets:
        print(f"✅ Found {len(tickets)} open RT tickets.")
    else:
        print("✅ No open RT tickets found.")

    return tickets

def is_alert_cleared(ticket_id):
    """Checks if the latest comment on an RT ticket indicates the alert is cleared."""
    logging.info(f"🔎 Checking RT ticket #{ticket_id} for cleared alert status...")

    try:
        latest_comment = rt_api.get_latest_ticket_comment(ticket_id)

        if not latest_comment:
            logging.info(f"⚠️ No recent comments found for RT ticket #{ticket_id}. Assuming NOT cleared.")
            return False

        latest_comment = latest_comment.strip().lower()

        # ✅ Check for both clear phrases
        if "the following has cleared:" in latest_comment or "severity: clear" in latest_comment:
            logging.info(f"✅ Alert in RT ticket #{ticket_id} is cleared.")
            return True
        else:
            logging.info(f"❌ Alert in RT ticket #{ticket_id} is NOT cleared.")
            return False

    except Exception as e:
        logging.error(f"❌ Error checking alert status for RT ticket #{ticket_id}: {e}")
        return False

def close_ticket(ticket_id):
    """Resolves and closes an RT ticket if the alert is cleared."""
    print(f"🔒 Closing RT ticket #{ticket_id}...")

    if rt_api.resolve_ticket(ticket_id):
        rt_api.add_comment(ticket_id, "✅ Alert has been cleared. Auto-closing ticket.")
        print(f"✅ RT ticket #{ticket_id} successfully closed.")
    else:
        print(f"❌ Failed to close RT ticket #{ticket_id}.")

def process_tickets():
    """Processes all open RT tickets and closes those with cleared alerts."""
    logging.info("🚀 Starting RT ticket processing...")
    
    # ✅ Fetch open tickets from the correct queue
    tickets = rt_api.get_open_tickets(queue_name="SOC Alerts")

    if not tickets:
        logging.info("✅ No open RT tickets found. Exiting...")
        print("✅ No open RT tickets found.")
        return

    # ✅ Debugging: Show all open ticket IDs being checked
    print(f"🔍 Checking {len(tickets)} open RT tickets...")
    logging.info(f"🔍 Checking {len(tickets)} open RT tickets...")

    for ticket_id in tickets:
        print(f"🔎 Checking RT Ticket #{ticket_id}...")
        
        if is_alert_cleared(ticket_id):
            print(f"✅ Closing RT Ticket #{ticket_id} (Alert Cleared)...")
            close_ticket(ticket_id)

    logging.info("✅ All cleared RT tickets processed successfully!")
    print("✔ RT Queue Processing Complete!")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    process_tickets()




"""
RT API Helper Module (CLI-Only)
-----------------------------------------
Provides helper functions to interact with the RT (Request Tracker) API.

🛠️ Features:
- Adds comments to RT tickets.
- Fetches ticket details.
- Retrieves open SOC tickets.
- Checks latest ticket comments.
- Resolves tickets.
- Logs all interactions in Logs/SOC_RT_API_Log.txt.

✅ Designed for CLI operation with SOC scripts.
"""

import requests
import logging
import os


# ✅ Setup Logging in Logs Directory
BASE_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))  # Get script directory
LOG_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "..", "Logs")  # Store logs in central location
os.makedirs(LOG_DIR, exist_ok=True)  # Create Logs directory if missing
LOG_FILE = os.path.join(LOG_DIR, "SOC_RT_API_Log.txt")

logging.basicConfig(filename=LOG_FILE, format='%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s', level=logging.INFO)

# 🔧 RT API Configuration
RT_URL = "https://rt.marchex.com/REST/1.0"
RT_USER = "socbot"
RT_PASS = "securepass"

import requests
import ssl
import urllib3

# ✅ Disable SSL verification warnings
urllib3.disable_warnings(urllib3.exceptions.InsecureRequestWarning)

# ✅ Override SSL settings globally (allows weaker DH keys)
try:
    ssl_context = ssl.create_default_context()
    ssl_context.set_ciphers("DEFAULT:@SECLEVEL=1")  # Allow weak keys
    requests.packages.urllib3.util.ssl_.DEFAULT_CIPHERS = "DEFAULT:@SECLEVEL=1"
except Exception as e:
    print(f"⚠️ Failed to override SSL settings: {e}")

# ✅ Custom SSL context to allow weak DH keys
custom_ssl_context = ssl.create_default_context()
custom_ssl_context.set_ciphers("DEFAULT:@SECLEVEL=1")  # Allow weaker SSL keys

# ✅ Create a requests session with modified SSL settings
session = requests.Session()
adapter = requests.adapters.HTTPAdapter()
session.mount("https://", adapter)


def _send_request(method, endpoint, data=None):
    """
    Sends an authenticated request to the RT API.

    Args:
        method (str): "GET" or "POST".
        endpoint (str): The RT API endpoint.
        data (dict, optional): Request payload.

    Returns:
        str: Response text if successful, None otherwise.
    """
    url = f"{RT_URL}{endpoint}"
    print(f"📡 Sending {method} request to: {url}")  # Debugging output

    try:
        response = session.request(
            method,
            url,
            auth=(RT_USER, RT_PASS),
            data=data,
            timeout=10,
            verify=False  # ✅ Ignore SSL verification
        )

        # ✅ Debugging: Print the full HTTP response
        print(f"🔍 Response Status Code: {response.status_code}")
        print(f"🔍 Response Text:\n{response.text}")

        if response.status_code == 200:
            return response.text
        else:
            logging.error(f"❌ RT API request failed: {response.text}")
            return None

    except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
        logging.error(f"❌ Request error: {e}")
        print(f"❌ Request error: {e}")  # Debugging output
        return None

def add_comment(ticket_number, comment):
    """Adds a comment to an RT ticket."""
    if not ticket_number or not comment.strip():
        logging.warning(f"⚠️ Missing ticket number or empty comment for RT Ticket #{ticket_number}.")
        return False

    response = _send_request("POST", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/comment", {"content": comment})
    return bool(response)

def get_ticket_details(ticket_number):
    """Retrieves details of an RT ticket."""
    return _send_request("GET", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/show")

def get_open_tickets(queue_name="SOC Alerts"):
    """
    Fetches all open tickets in a given RT queue.

    Args:
        queue_name (str, optional): The RT queue name (default: "SOC Alerts").

    Returns:
        list: List of open ticket IDs, or an empty list if none found.
    """

    logging.info(f"🔍 Fetching open tickets in RT queue '{queue_name}'...")

    # ✅ Debugging: Print the exact query being sent
    query = f"Queue='{queue_name}' AND (Status='open' OR Status='new' OR Status='stalled')"
    print(f"📡 RT API Query: {query}")  # Debugging output

    response = _send_request("GET", f"/search/ticket?query={query}")

    # ✅ Debugging: Print raw API response
    print("🔍 Raw API Response:\n", response)  

    if response:
        # ✅ Extract ticket IDs from the RT response
        tickets = [line.split(":")[0].strip() for line in response.split("\n") if line.strip()]
        print(f"✅ Extracted Tickets: {tickets}")  # ✅ Debugging output
        logging.info(f"✅ Found {len(tickets)} open tickets in queue '{queue_name}'.")
        return tickets
    else:
        logging.error(f"❌ Failed to fetch open tickets from queue '{queue_name}'.")
        return []

def get_latest_ticket_comment(ticket_number):
    """Retrieves the latest comment from an RT ticket."""
    response = _send_request("GET", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/history?format=l")

    if response:
        comments = response.split("\n")
        latest_comment = comments[-1].strip() if comments else ""
        print(f"📝 Latest Comment for Ticket {ticket_number}: {latest_comment}")  # ✅ Debugging output
        return latest_comment
    else:
        logging.error(f"❌ Failed to retrieve comments for RT Ticket #{ticket_number}.")
        return None

def resolve_ticket(ticket_number):
    """Resolves an RT ticket by setting its status to 'resolved'."""
    return bool(_send_request("POST", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/edit", {"Status": "resolved"}))

if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Example test: fetch open tickets
    print("Fetching open tickets...")
    open_tickets = get_open_tickets()
    print(f"Open Tickets: {open_tickets}")

    except Exception as e:

        return False

        print(f"✅ RT ticket #{ticket_id} successfully closed.")

    """Processes all open RT tickets and closes those with cleared alerts."""
    logging.info("🚀 Starting RT ticket processing...")
    
    # ✅ Fetch open tickets from the correct queue

"""
SOC RT Ticket Auto-Close Script (CLI Only)
-----------------------------------------
Automatically checks open RT tickets in the SOC Alerts queue
and closes them if the related alert has been cleared.

🛠️ Features:
- Fetches all open RT tickets.
- Checks the latest comment for "clear" keywords.
- If cleared, resolves & closes the ticket automatically.
- Logs all actions in Logs/SOC_RTs_Log.txt.
✅ Fully automated with error handling. Designed for CLI operation.
"""

import logging
import os
import sys

# ✅ Ensure input/output uses UTF-8 (prevents UnicodeEncodeError & DecodeError)
sys.stdout.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")
sys.stderr.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")
sys.stdin.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")

# Ensure Utils is accessible for rt_api.py
BASE_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))  # Get script directory
UTILS_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Utils")  # Locate Utils folder
sys.path.append(UTILS_DIR)  # Add to system path

import rt_api  # RT API wrapper

# ✅ Setup Logging in Logs Directory
LOG_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Logs")
os.makedirs(LOG_DIR, exist_ok=True)  # Create Logs directory if missing
LOG_FILE = os.path.join(LOG_DIR, "SOC_RTs_Log.txt")

logging.basicConfig(filename=LOG_FILE, format='%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s', level=logging.INFO)

# ✅ Keywords used to identify a cleared alert
CLEAR_KEYWORDS = ["cleared", "alert cleared", "resolved", "no further action needed"]

def get_open_tickets():
    """Fetches open alert tickets from RT."""
    print("🔍 Fetching open RT tickets...")
    tickets = rt_api.get_open_tickets()

    if tickets:
        print(f"✅ Found {len(tickets)} open RT tickets.")
    else:
        print("✅ No open RT tickets found.")

    return tickets

def is_alert_cleared(ticket_id):
    """Checks if the latest comment on an RT ticket indicates the alert is cleared."""
    logging.info(f"🔎 Checking RT ticket #{ticket_id} for cleared alert status...")

    try:
        latest_comment = rt_api.get_latest_ticket_comment(ticket_id)

        if not latest_comment:
            logging.info(f"⚠️ No recent comments found for RT ticket #{ticket_id}. Assuming NOT cleared.")
            return False

        latest_comment = latest_comment.strip().lower()

        # ✅ Check for both clear phrases
        if "the following has cleared:" in latest_comment or "severity: clear" in latest_comment:
            logging.info(f"✅ Alert in RT ticket #{ticket_id} is cleared.")
            return True
        else:
            logging.info(f"❌ Alert in RT ticket #{ticket_id} is NOT cleared.")
            return False

    except Exception as e:
        logging.error(f"❌ Error checking alert status for RT ticket #{ticket_id}: {e}")
        return False

def close_ticket(ticket_id):
    """Resolves and closes an RT ticket if the alert is cleared."""
    print(f"🔒 Closing RT ticket #{ticket_id}...")

    if rt_api.resolve_ticket(ticket_id):
        rt_api.add_comment(ticket_id, "✅ Alert has been cleared. Auto-closing ticket.")
        print(f"✅ RT ticket #{ticket_id} successfully closed.")
    else:
        print(f"❌ Failed to close RT ticket #{ticket_id}.")

def process_tickets():
    """Processes all open RT tickets and closes those with cleared alerts."""
    logging.info("🚀 Starting RT ticket processing...")
    
    # ✅ Fetch open tickets from the correct queue
    tickets = rt_api.get_open_tickets(queue_name="SOC Alerts")

    if not tickets:
        logging.info("✅ No open RT tickets found. Exiting...")
        print("✅ No open RT tickets found.")
        return

    # ✅ Debugging: Show all open ticket IDs being checked
    print(f"🔍 Checking {len(tickets)} open RT tickets...")
    logging.info(f"🔍 Checking {len(tickets)} open RT tickets...")

    for ticket_id in tickets:
        print(f"🔎 Checking RT Ticket #{ticket_id}...")
        
        if is_alert_cleared(ticket_id):
            print(f"✅ Closing RT Ticket #{ticket_id} (Alert Cleared)...")
            close_ticket(ticket_id)

    logging.info("✅ All cleared RT tickets processed successfully!")
    print("✔ RT Queue Processing Complete!")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    process_tickets()




"""
RT API Helper Module (CLI-Only)
-----------------------------------------
Provides helper functions to interact with the RT (Request Tracker) API.

🛠️ Features:
- Adds comments to RT tickets.
- Fetches ticket details.
- Retrieves open SOC tickets.
- Checks latest ticket comments.
- Resolves tickets.
- Logs all interactions in Logs/SOC_RT_API_Log.txt.

✅ Designed for CLI operation with SOC scripts.
"""

import requests
import logging
import os


# ✅ Setup Logging in Logs Directory
BASE_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))  # Get script directory
LOG_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "..", "Logs")  # Store logs in central location
os.makedirs(LOG_DIR, exist_ok=True)  # Create Logs directory if missing
LOG_FILE = os.path.join(LOG_DIR, "SOC_RT_API_Log.txt")

logging.basicConfig(filename=LOG_FILE, format='%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s', level=logging.INFO)

# 🔧 RT API Configuration
RT_URL = "https://rt.marchex.com/REST/1.0"
RT_USER = "socbot"
RT_PASS = "securepass"

import requests
import ssl
import urllib3

# ✅ Disable SSL verification warnings
urllib3.disable_warnings(urllib3.exceptions.InsecureRequestWarning)

# ✅ Override SSL settings globally (allows weaker DH keys)
try:
    ssl_context = ssl.create_default_context()
    ssl_context.set_ciphers("DEFAULT:@SECLEVEL=1")  # Allow weak keys
    requests.packages.urllib3.util.ssl_.DEFAULT_CIPHERS = "DEFAULT:@SECLEVEL=1"
except Exception as e:
    print(f"⚠️ Failed to override SSL settings: {e}")

# ✅ Custom SSL context to allow weak DH keys
custom_ssl_context = ssl.create_default_context()
custom_ssl_context.set_ciphers("DEFAULT:@SECLEVEL=1")  # Allow weaker SSL keys

# ✅ Create a requests session with modified SSL settings
session = requests.Session()
adapter = requests.adapters.HTTPAdapter()
session.mount("https://", adapter)


def _send_request(method, endpoint, data=None):
    """
    Sends an authenticated request to the RT API.

    Args:
        method (str): "GET" or "POST".
        endpoint (str): The RT API endpoint.
        data (dict, optional): Request payload.

    Returns:
        str: Response text if successful, None otherwise.
    """
    url = f"{RT_URL}{endpoint}"
    print(f"📡 Sending {method} request to: {url}")  # Debugging output

    try:
        response = session.request(
            method,
            url,
            auth=(RT_USER, RT_PASS),
            data=data,
            timeout=10,
            verify=False  # ✅ Ignore SSL verification
        )

        # ✅ Debugging: Print the full HTTP response
        print(f"🔍 Response Status Code: {response.status_code}")
        print(f"🔍 Response Text:\n{response.text}")

        if response.status_code == 200:
            return response.text
        else:
            logging.error(f"❌ RT API request failed: {response.text}")
            return None

    except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
        logging.error(f"❌ Request error: {e}")
        print(f"❌ Request error: {e}")  # Debugging output
        return None

def add_comment(ticket_number, comment):
    """Adds a comment to an RT ticket."""
    if not ticket_number or not comment.strip():
        logging.warning(f"⚠️ Missing ticket number or empty comment for RT Ticket #{ticket_number}.")
        return False

    response = _send_request("POST", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/comment", {"content": comment})
    return bool(response)

def get_ticket_details(ticket_number):
    """Retrieves details of an RT ticket."""
    return _send_request("GET", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/show")

def get_open_tickets(queue_name="SOC Alerts"):
    """
    Fetches all open tickets in a given RT queue.

    Args:
        queue_name (str, optional): The RT queue name (default: "SOC Alerts").

    Returns:
        list: List of open ticket IDs, or an empty list if none found.
    """

    logging.info(f"🔍 Fetching open tickets in RT queue '{queue_name}'...")

    # ✅ Debugging: Print the exact query being sent
    query = f"Queue='{queue_name}' AND (Status='open' OR Status='new' OR Status='stalled')"
    print(f"📡 RT API Query: {query}")  # Debugging output

    response = _send_request("GET", f"/search/ticket?query={query}")

    # ✅ Debugging: Print raw API response
    print("🔍 Raw API Response:\n", response)  

    if response:
        # ✅ Extract ticket IDs from the RT response
        tickets = [line.split(":")[0].strip() for line in response.split("\n") if line.strip()]
        print(f"✅ Extracted Tickets: {tickets}")  # ✅ Debugging output
        logging.info(f"✅ Found {len(tickets)} open tickets in queue '{queue_name}'.")
        return tickets
    else:
        logging.error(f"❌ Failed to fetch open tickets from queue '{queue_name}'.")
        return []

def get_latest_ticket_comment(ticket_number):
    """Retrieves the latest comment from an RT ticket."""
    response = _send_request("GET", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/history?format=l")

    if response:
        comments = response.split("\n")
        latest_comment = comments[-1].strip() if comments else ""
        print(f"📝 Latest Comment for Ticket {ticket_number}: {latest_comment}")  # ✅ Debugging output
        return latest_comment
    else:
        logging.error(f"❌ Failed to retrieve comments for RT Ticket #{ticket_number}.")
        return None

def resolve_ticket(ticket_number):
    """Resolves an RT ticket by setting its status to 'resolved'."""
    return bool(_send_request("POST", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/edit", {"Status": "resolved"}))

if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Example test: fetch open tickets
    print("Fetching open tickets...")
    open_tickets = get_open_tickets()
    print(f"Open Tickets: {open_tickets}")

"""
SOC RT Ticket Auto-Close Script (CLI Only)
-----------------------------------------
Automatically checks open RT tickets in the SOC Alerts queue
and closes them if the related alert has been cleared.

🛠️ Features:
- Fetches all open RT tickets.
- Checks the latest comment for "clear" keywords.
- If cleared, resolves & closes the ticket automatically.
- Logs all actions in Logs/SOC_RTs_Log.txt.
✅ Fully automated with error handling. Designed for CLI operation.
"""

import logging
import os
import sys

# ✅ Ensure input/output uses UTF-8 (prevents UnicodeEncodeError & DecodeError)
sys.stdout.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")
sys.stderr.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")
sys.stdin.reconfigure(encoding="utf-8")

# Ensure Utils is accessible for rt_api.py
BASE_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))  # Get script directory
UTILS_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Utils")  # Locate Utils folder
sys.path.append(UTILS_DIR)  # Add to system path

import rt_api  # RT API wrapper

# ✅ Setup Logging in Logs Directory
LOG_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "Logs")
os.makedirs(LOG_DIR, exist_ok=True)  # Create Logs directory if missing
LOG_FILE = os.path.join(LOG_DIR, "SOC_RTs_Log.txt")

logging.basicConfig(filename=LOG_FILE, format='%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s', level=logging.INFO)

# ✅ Keywords used to identify a cleared alert
CLEAR_KEYWORDS = ["cleared", "alert cleared", "resolved", "no further action needed"]

def get_open_tickets():
    """Fetches open alert tickets from RT."""
    print("🔍 Fetching open RT tickets...")
    tickets = rt_api.get_open_tickets()

    if tickets:
        print(f"✅ Found {len(tickets)} open RT tickets.")
    else:
        print("✅ No open RT tickets found.")

    return tickets

def is_alert_cleared(ticket_id):
    """Checks if the latest comment on an RT ticket indicates the alert is cleared."""
    logging.info(f"🔎 Checking RT ticket #{ticket_id} for cleared alert status...")

    try:
        latest_comment = rt_api.get_latest_ticket_comment(ticket_id)

        if not latest_comment:
            logging.info(f"⚠️ No recent comments found for RT ticket #{ticket_id}. Assuming NOT cleared.")
            return False

        latest_comment = latest_comment.strip().lower()

        # ✅ Check for both clear phrases
        if "the following has cleared:" in latest_comment or "severity: clear" in latest_comment:
            logging.info(f"✅ Alert in RT ticket #{ticket_id} is cleared.")
            return True
        else:
            logging.info(f"❌ Alert in RT ticket #{ticket_id} is NOT cleared.")
            return False

    except Exception as e:
        logging.error(f"❌ Error checking alert status for RT ticket #{ticket_id}: {e}")
        return False

def close_ticket(ticket_id):
    """Resolves and closes an RT ticket if the alert is cleared."""
    print(f"🔒 Closing RT ticket #{ticket_id}...")

    if rt_api.resolve_ticket(ticket_id):
        rt_api.add_comment(ticket_id, "✅ Alert has been cleared. Auto-closing ticket.")
        print(f"✅ RT ticket #{ticket_id} successfully closed.")
    else:
        print(f"❌ Failed to close RT ticket #{ticket_id}.")

def process_tickets():
    """Processes all open RT tickets and closes those with cleared alerts."""
    logging.info("🚀 Starting RT ticket processing...")
    
    # ✅ Fetch open tickets from the correct queue
    tickets = rt_api.get_open_tickets(queue_name="SOC Alerts")

    if not tickets:
        logging.info("✅ No open RT tickets found. Exiting...")
        print("✅ No open RT tickets found.")
        return

    # ✅ Debugging: Show all open ticket IDs being checked
    print(f"🔍 Checking {len(tickets)} open RT tickets...")
    logging.info(f"🔍 Checking {len(tickets)} open RT tickets...")

    for ticket_id in tickets:
        print(f"🔎 Checking RT Ticket #{ticket_id}...")
        
        if is_alert_cleared(ticket_id):
            print(f"✅ Closing RT Ticket #{ticket_id} (Alert Cleared)...")
            close_ticket(ticket_id)

    logging.info("✅ All cleared RT tickets processed successfully!")
    print("✔ RT Queue Processing Complete!")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    process_tickets()




"""
RT API Helper Module (CLI-Only)
-----------------------------------------
Provides helper functions to interact with the RT (Request Tracker) API.

🛠️ Features:
- Adds comments to RT tickets.
- Fetches ticket details.
- Retrieves open SOC tickets.
- Checks latest ticket comments.
- Resolves tickets.
- Logs all interactions in Logs/SOC_RT_API_Log.txt.

✅ Designed for CLI operation with SOC scripts.
"""

import requests
import logging
import os


# ✅ Setup Logging in Logs Directory
BASE_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__))  # Get script directory
LOG_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, "..", "Logs")  # Store logs in central location
os.makedirs(LOG_DIR, exist_ok=True)  # Create Logs directory if missing
LOG_FILE = os.path.join(LOG_DIR, "SOC_RT_API_Log.txt")

logging.basicConfig(filename=LOG_FILE, format='%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s', level=logging.INFO)

# 🔧 RT API Configuration
RT_URL = "https://rt.marchex.com/REST/1.0"
RT_USER = "socbot"
RT_PASS = "securepass"

import requests
import ssl
import urllib3

# Force OpenSSL to use SECLEVEL=1 (allows weak DH keys)
ssl._create_default_https_context = ssl._create_unverified_context

# ✅ Disable SSL verification warnings
urllib3.disable_warnings(urllib3.exceptions.InsecureRequestWarning)

# ✅ Override SSL settings globally (allows weaker DH keys)
try:
    ssl_context = ssl.create_default_context()
    ssl_context.set_ciphers("DEFAULT:@SECLEVEL=1")  # Allow weak DH keys
    ssl_context.check_hostname = False
    ssl_context.verify_mode = ssl.CERT_NONE  # Bypass cert verification (only if needed)
    requests.packages.urllib3.util.ssl_.DEFAULT_CIPHERS = "DEFAULT:@SECLEVEL=1"
except Exception as e:
    print(f"⚠️ Failed to override SSL settings: {e}")

# ✅ Custom SSL context to allow weak DH keys
custom_ssl_context = ssl.create_default_context()
custom_ssl_context.set_ciphers("DEFAULT:@SECLEVEL=1")  # Allow weaker SSL keys


def _send_request(method, endpoint, data=None):
    """
    Sends an authenticated request to the RT API.

    Args:
        method (str): "GET" or "POST".
        endpoint (str): The RT API endpoint.
        data (dict, optional): Request payload.

    Returns:
        str: Response text if successful, None otherwise.
    """
    url = f"https://rt.marchex.com/REST/1.0{endpoint}"
    print(f"📡 Sending {method} request to: {url}")  # Debugging output

    try:
        session = requests.Session()
        adapter = requests.adapters.HTTPAdapter()
        session.mount("https://", adapter)

        # ✅ Override SSL settings to allow weak DH keys
        response = requests.request(
            method,
            url,
            auth=("socbot", "securepass"),
            data=data,
            timeout=10,
            verify=False,  # Ignore SSL cert verification
            cert=None,
            headers={"User-Agent": "Mozilla/5.0"},
        )

        # ✅ Debugging: Print the full HTTP response
        print(f"🔍 Response Status Code: {response.status_code}")
        print(f"🔍 Response Text:\n{response.text}")

        if response.status_code == 200:
            return response.text
        else:
            print(f"❌ RT API request failed: {response.text}")
            logging.error(f"❌ RT API request failed: {response.text}")
            return None

    except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
        logging.error(f"❌ Request error: {e}")
        print(f"❌ Request error: {e}")  # Debugging output
        return None

def add_comment(ticket_number, comment):
    """Adds a comment to an RT ticket."""
    if not ticket_number or not comment.strip():
        logging.warning(f"⚠️ Missing ticket number or empty comment for RT Ticket #{ticket_number}.")
        return False

    response = _send_request("POST", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/comment", {"content": comment})
    return bool(response)

def get_ticket_details(ticket_number):
    """Retrieves details of an RT ticket."""
    return _send_request("GET", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/show")

def get_open_tickets(queue_name="SOC Alerts"):
    """
    Fetches all open tickets in a given RT queue.

    Args:
        queue_name (str, optional): The RT queue name (default: "SOC Alerts").

    Returns:
        list: List of open ticket IDs, or an empty list if none found.
    """

    logging.info(f"🔍 Fetching open tickets in RT queue '{queue_name}'...")

    # ✅ Debugging: Print the exact query being sent
    query = f"Queue='{queue_name}' AND (Status='open' OR Status='new' OR Status='stalled')"
    print(f"📡 RT API Query: {query}")  # Debugging output

    response = _send_request("GET", f"/search/ticket?query={query}")

    # ✅ Debugging: Print raw API response
    print("🔍 Raw API Response:\n", response)  

    if response:
        # ✅ Extract ticket IDs from the RT response
        tickets = [line.split(":")[0].strip() for line in response.split("\n") if line.strip()]
        print(f"✅ Extracted Tickets: {tickets}")  # ✅ Debugging output
        logging.info(f"✅ Found {len(tickets)} open tickets in queue '{queue_name}'.")
        return tickets
    else:
        logging.error(f"❌ Failed to fetch open tickets from queue '{queue_name}'.")
        return []

def get_latest_ticket_comment(ticket_number):
    """Retrieves the latest comment from an RT ticket."""
    response = _send_request("GET", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/history?format=l")

    if response:
        comments = response.split("\n")
        latest_comment = comments[-1].strip() if comments else ""
        print(f"📝 Latest Comment for Ticket {ticket_number}: {latest_comment}")  # ✅ Debugging output
        return latest_comment
    else:
        logging.error(f"❌ Failed to retrieve comments for RT Ticket #{ticket_number}.")
        return None

def resolve_ticket(ticket_number):
    """Resolves an RT ticket by setting its status to 'resolved'."""
    return bool(_send_request("POST", f"/ticket/{ticket_number}/edit", {"Status": "resolved"}))

if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Example test: fetch open tickets
    print("Fetching open tickets...")
    open_tickets = get_open_tickets()
    print(f"Open Tickets: {open_tickets}")

import logging
import psycopg2
import secret

# Setup logging
logging.basicConfig(
    format="%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s",
    level=logging.INFO
)

# Database configuration
DB_CONFIG = {
    "dbname": "adtrack_ro",
    "host": "vspool.som1.marchex.com",
    "port": 5432,
    "user": secret.get_secret("_ADTRACK_DB_USER"),
    "password": secret.get_secret("_ADTRACK_DB_PASS")
}

def get_db_connection(mock_mode):
    """Establish a connection to the AdTrack database."""
    if mock_mode:
        logging.info("[MOCK] Skipping real DB connection.")
        return None  # Avoid actual database connections

    try:
        conn = psycopg2.connect(**DB_CONFIG)
        return conn
    except Exception as e:
        logging.error(f"Database connection failed: {e}")
        return None

def main(user, creds):
    """Check or remove AdTrack access for a given user."""
    mock_mode = creds["MOCK_MODE"]  # Read from the separations script

    if creds["vendorEmail"]:
        search_param = creds["vendorEmail"]
    else:
        search_param = f"{user}@marchex%"

    if mock_mode:
        logging.info(f"[MOCK] Simulating DB lookup for {search_param}")
        # Simulate finding the user
        found_users = [f"{user}@marchex.com"]
        return found_users, user, creds if found_users else (None, user, creds)

    conn = get_db_connection(mock_mode)
    if not conn:
        return None, user, creds

    query = "SELECT email FROM at_user WHERE email ILIKE %s AND status != 'disabled'"
    try:
        with conn.cursor() as cur:
            cur.execute(query, (search_param,))
            rows = cur.fetchall()

        conn.close()
        return [row[0] for row in rows] if rows else None, user, creds

    except Exception as e:
        logging.error(f"Database query failed: {e}")
        return None, user, creds

def remove_access(user, mock_mode):
    """Attempt to remove user access from AdTrack."""
    if mock_mode:
        logging.info(f"[MOCK] Would remove access for {user} in AdTrack.")
        return  # No real DB actions

    conn = get_db_connection(mock_mode)
    if not conn:
        return

    delete_query = "UPDATE at_user SET status = 'disabled' WHERE email ILIKE %s"
    try:
        with conn.cursor() as cur:
            cur.execute(delete_query, (f"{user}@marchex%",))
            conn.commit()
        logging.info(f"Access removed for {user} in AdTrack.")

    except Exception as e:
        logging.error(f"Failed to remove AdTrack access for {user}: {e}")

    finally:
        if conn:
            conn.close()

def foundAccess(result):
    """Handle access check and potential removal."""
    if result[0]:
        user = result[1]
        accessChoice = result[2]["accessChoice"]
        mock_mode = result[2]["MOCK_MODE"]  # Read from separations.py

        if accessChoice == "check":
            logging.info(f"{user} has AdTrack UI access.")
        elif accessChoice == "remove":
            logging.info(f"{user} has AdTrack UI access. Attempting removal...")
            remove_access(user, mock_mode)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    sepList = input("Enter LDAP user(s) to be separated (comma-separated): ").split(",")
    accessChoice = input("Would you like to check or remove access? (Check/Remove): ").lower()
    isVendor = input("Is this user a vendor? (Yes/No): ").lower()

    while accessChoice not in ("remove", "check"):
        accessChoice = input("Invalid input. Please enter 'Remove' or 'Check': ").strip().lower()

    vendorEmail = None
    if isVendor == "yes":
        vendorEmail = input("Enter vendor email address: ")

    creds = {
        "accessChoice": accessChoice,
        "vendorEmail": vendorEmail,
        "MOCK_MODE": True  # This is just for standalone testing; separations.py will override this
    }

    for user in sepList:
        result = main(user.strip(), creds)
        foundAccess(result)




heres the current check_adtrack.py script and the SOP for adtrack access





SOC SOP uiAccessAdTrack
SOC SOP uiAccessAdTrack
Jump to navigationJump to search

Contents
1	Description
2	Adding Access
2.1	If the user doesn't ask for "Staff level", email them asking them if they do and make sure to give them the URL for Adtrack Account standards to help them
2.1.1	NOTE
3	Removing Access
Description
This SOP is for adding and removing access for the Adtrack UI, aka Marchex.IO

Adding AccessRemoving Access

When an account needs to be added by request/ticket use the following steps.


If a user requests access to the Adtrack UI also called Marchex.io and need access to the tool. Most of our requests are for "staff level" access. See "Adtrack Account standards" link below

Adtrack Account standards 
If the user doesn't ask for "Staff level", email them asking them if they do and make sure to give them the URL for Adtrack Account standards to help them
http://wiki.marchex.com/index.php/SOC_SOP_adtrackUIAccountStandards

1. Log into Adtrack

Service Account & Password found in Bitwarden

2. Click the Client List tab in the UI.

3. Unless specified in the ticket create their account in the following group:

Marchex Voice Services (nee Voicestar) (This has been the historic place to put accounts for Marchex users.)

Note:

Sometimes you will have to match an account with another account.
The easiest way to do that is to open a two tabs in your browser.
In the first one, search in "Client list" using the target email (user to copy)
Then follow the below steps and just match up all the permissions.
4. Click on the Account Name, it will drop down, and click Account Settings.

5. Click Users

6. Click "New user".

7. Fill in the user's information:

Real Name
Email
Password [Password Gen]
NOTE:

If the email account is already in use, the tool will not let you use it again. You either have to alter the email with a Capital letter or find the other account and update that one.

8. Click submit at the bottom.

9. Search for the users account once more to provision it.

10. Using either given credentials from another account (Not preferred method) or [staff level] provision the account and click "update" at the bottom.

There are three specific pieces that Require more than the users manager approval: Bulk create /update Campaigns & accounts, Billing Write , and Edit Staff Permissions . See above staff level link.

11. Email the credentials to the user.


NOTE
Adtrack staff tools exist Here and will soon (hopefully) have a staff search function, at which point the above instructions will be thankfully obsolete.
